Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which the rolling median is computed. Only windows that fit\n            fully inside the array are included.\n        'same'\n            Output has the same length as the input along `axis`.  Windows\n            near the edges are padded with ``np.nan`` when the input has a\n            floating-point dtype, or centered as much as possible.\n        'full'\n            Output has length ``N + window_size - 1``.  The window slides\n            from a position where only the last element overlaps to one\n            where only the first element overlaps.\n\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    out : ndarray\n        Array of rolling medians.  Has the same shape as `a` except along\n        `axis`, where its length depends on `mode`.\n\n    Raises\n    ------\n    ValueError\n        If `window_size` is not a positive integer, if `mode` is not one of\n        'valid', 'same', or 'full', or if `axis` is out of bounds.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 3, 2, 5, 4])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([2., 2., 3., 4., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 2. , 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 4. ])\n\n    With window_size=1, the output equals the input:\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 1)\n    array([1., 3., 2., 5., 4.])\n\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asarray(a)\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)) or window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\n            \"window_size must be a positive integer, got %r\" % window_size\n        )\n    window_size = int(window_size)\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(\n            \"mode must be 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got %r\" % mode\n        )\n\n    # Normalise axis\n    nd = a.ndim\n    if nd == 0:\n        a = a[np.newaxis]\n        nd = 1\n    axis = np.lib._array_utils_impl.normalize_axis_index(axis, nd)\n\n    n = a.shape[axis]\n\n    # Determine padding required for each mode\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        pad_before = 0\n        pad_after = 0\n        out_len = max(0, n - window_size + 1)\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        pad_before = (window_size - 1) // 2\n        pad_after = window_size - 1 - pad_before\n        out_len = n\n    else:  # 'full'\n        pad_before = window_size - 1\n        pad_after = window_size - 1\n        out_len = n + window_size - 1\n\n    if out_len == 0:\n        # Build an empty output with the correct shape\n        out_shape = list(a.shape)\n        out_shape[axis] = 0\n        return np.empty(out_shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Pad the array with NaN along the chosen axis when needed\n    if pad_before > 0 or pad_after > 0:\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * nd\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n        # Use float so NaN padding is valid\n        a_float = a.astype(np.float64, copy=False)\n        a_padded = np.pad(a_float, pad_width, mode='constant',\n                          constant_values=np.nan)\n    else:\n        a_padded = a.astype(np.float64, copy=False)\n\n    padded_len = a_padded.shape[axis]\n\n    # Build the output by iterating over windows\n    out_shape = list(a_padded.shape)\n    out_shape[axis] = out_len\n    out = np.empty(out_shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Use np.median (which handles NaN via ignoring if using nanmedian) for\n    # each window slice along the axis.\n    # For modes with NaN padding we use np.nanmedian.\n    _median_func = np.nanmedian if (pad_before > 0 or pad_after > 0) else np.median\n\n    for i in range(out_len):\n        sl = [slice(None)] * nd\n        sl[axis] = slice(i, i + window_size)\n        window_data = a_padded[tuple(sl)]\n        out_sl = [slice(None)] * nd\n        out_sl[axis] = i\n        out[tuple(out_sl)] = _median_func(window_data, axis=axis)\n\n    return out\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":568,"cache_read_input_tokens":39413,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":568,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"26b68026-f70b-48a2-8275-deaa202b41f7","uuid":"6d72849d-9025-4e70-bbf6-5c1b59b98624"}

1\n        pad_after = window_size - 1\n        out_len = n + window_size - 1\n\n    if out_len == 0:\n        # Build an empty output with the correct shape\n        out_shape = list(a.shape)\n        out_shape[axis] = 0\n        return np.empty(out_shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Pad the array with NaN along the chosen axis when needed\n    if pad_before > 0 or pad_after > 0:\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * nd\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n        # Use float so NaN padding is valid\n        a_float = a.astype(np.float64, copy=False)\n        a_padded = np.pad(a_float, pad_width, mode='constant',\n                          constant_values=np.nan)\n    else:\n        a_padded = a.astype(np.float64, copy=False)\n\n    padded_len = a_padded.shape[axis]\n\n    # Build the output by iterating over windows\n    out_shape = list(a_padded.shape)\n    out_shape[axis] = out_len\n    out = np.empty(out_shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Use np.median (which handles NaN via ignoring if using nanmedian) for\n    # each window slice along the axis.\n    # For modes with NaN padding we use np.nanmedian.\n    _median_func = np.nanmedian if (pad_before > 0 or pad_after > 0) else np.median\n\n    for i in range(out_len):\n        sl = [slice(None)] * nd\n        sl[axis] = slice(i, i + window_size)\n        window_data = a_padded[tuple(sl)]\n        out_sl = [slice(None)] * nd\n        out_sl[axis] = i\n        out[tuple(out_sl)] = _median_func(window_data, axis=axis)\n\n    return out\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which the rolling median is computed. Default is -1\n        (the last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the length of the output:\n\n        'valid'\n            Output has length ``max(0, N - window_size + 1)``, where ``N``\n            is the length of the input along `axis`.  Only windows that fit\n            fully inside the array are included.\n        'same'\n            Output has the same length as the input along `axis`.  Windows\n            near the edges are padded with ``np.nan`` when the input has a\n            floating-point dtype, or centered as much as possible.\n        'full'\n            Output has length ``N + window_size - 1``.  The window slides\n            from a position where only the last element overlaps to one\n            where only the first element overlaps.\n\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    out : ndarray\n        Array of rolling medians.  Has the same shape as `a` except along\n        `axis`, where its length depends on `mode`.\n\n    Raises\n    ------\n    ValueError\n        If `window_size` is not a positive integer, if `mode` is not one of\n        'valid', 'same', or 'full', or if `axis` is out of bounds.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 3, 2, 5, 4])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([2., 2., 3., 4., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 2. , 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 4. ])\n\n    With window_size=1, the output equals the input:\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 1)\n    array([1., 3., 2., 5., 4.])\n\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asarray(a)\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)) or window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\n            \"window_size must be a positive integer, got %r\" % window_size\n        )\n    window_size = int(window_size)\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(\n            \"mode must be 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got %r\" % mode\n        )\n\n    # Normalise axis\n    nd = a.ndim\n    if nd == 0:\n        a = a[np.newaxis]\n        nd = 1\n    axis = np.lib._array_utils_impl.normalize_axis_index(axis, nd)\n\n    n = a.shape[axis]\n\n    # Determine padding required for each mode\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        pad_before = 0\n        pad_after = 0\n        out_len = max(0, n - window_size + 1)\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        pad_before = (window_size - 1) // 2\n        pad_after = window_size - 1 - pad_before\n        out_len = n\n    else:  # 'full'\n        pad_before = window_size - 1\n        pad_after = window_size - 1\n        out_len = n + window_size - 1\n\n    if out_len == 0:\n        # Build an empty output with the correct shape\n        out_shape = list(a.shape)\n        out_shape[axis] = 0\n        return np.empty(out_shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Pad the array with NaN along the chosen axis when needed\n    if pad_before > 0 or pad_after > 0:\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * nd\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n        # Use float so NaN padding is valid\n        a_float = a.astype(np.float64, copy=False)\n        a_padded = np.pad(a_float, pad_width, mode='constant',\n                          constant_values=np.nan)\n    else:\n        a_padded = a.astype(np.float64, copy=False)\n\n    padded_len = a_padded.shape[axis]\n\n    # Build the output by iterating over windows\n    out_shape = list(a_padded.shape)\n    out_shape[axis] = out_len\n    out = np.empty(out_shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Use np.median (which handles NaN via ignoring if using nanmedian) for\n    # each window slice along the axis.\n    # For modes with NaN padding we use np.nanmedian.\n    _median_func = np.nanmedian if (pad_before > 0 or pad_after > 0) else np.median\n\n    for i in range(out_len):\n        sl = [slice(None)] * nd\n        sl[axis] = slice(i, i + window_size)\n        window_data = a_padded[tuple(sl)]\n        out_sl = [slice(None)] * nd\n        out_sl[axis] = i\n        out[tuple(out_sl)] = _median_func(window_data, axis=axis)\n\n    return out\n","numLines":160,"startLine":1,"totalLines":160}}}

Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which the rolling median is computed. Default is -1\n        (the last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the length of the output:\n\n        'valid'\n            Output has length ``max(0, N - window_size + 1)``, where ``N``\n            is the length of the input along `axis`.  Only windows that fit\n            fully inside the array are included.\n        'same'\n            Output has the same length as the input along `axis`.  Windows\n            near the edges are padded with ``np.nan`` when the input has a\n            floating-point dtype, or centered as much as possible.\n        'full'\n            Output has length ``N + window_size - 1``.  The window slides\n            from a position where only the last element overlaps to one\n            where only the first element overlaps.\n\n        Default is 'valid'.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    out : ndarray\n        Array of rolling medians. window_size + 1)\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        pad_before = (window_size - 1) // 2\n        pad_after = window_size - 1 - pad_before\n        out_len = n\n    else:  # 'full'\n        pad_before = window_size - Has the same shape as `a` except along\n        `axis`, where its length depends on `mode`.\n\n    Raises\n    ------\n    ValueError\n        If `window_size` is not a positive integer, if `mode` is not one of\n        'valid', 'same', or 'full', or if `axis` is out of bounds.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 3, 2, 5, 4])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([2., 2., 3., 4., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([1. , 2. , 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5, 4. ])\n\n    With window_size=1, the output equals the input:\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 1)\n    array([1., 3., 2., 5., 4.])\n\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asarray(a)\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)) or window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(\n            \"window_size must be a positive integer, got %r\" % window_size\n        )\n    window_size = int(window_size)\n\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(\n            \"mode must be 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got %r\" % mode\n        )\n\n    # Normalise axis\n    nd = a.ndim\n    if nd == 0:\n        a = a[np.newaxis]\n        nd = 1\n    axis = normalize_axis_index(axis, nd)\n\n    n = a.shape[axis]\n\n    # Determine padding required for each mode\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        pad_before = 0\n        pad_after = 0\n        out_len = max(0, n - window_size + 1)\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        pad_before = (window_size - 1) // 2\n        pad_after = window_size - 1 - pad_before\n        out_len = n\n    else:  # 'full'\n        pad_before = window_size - 1\n        pad_after = window_size - 1\n        out_len = n + window_size - 1\n\n    if out_len == 0:\n        # Build an empty output with the correct shape\n        out_shape = list(a.shape)\n        out_shape[axis] = 0\n        return np.empty(out_shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Pad the array with NaN along the chosen axis when needed\n    if pad_before > 0 or pad_after > 0:\n        pad_width = [(0, 0)] * nd\n        pad_width[axis] = (pad_before, pad_after)\n        # Use float so NaN padding is valid\n        a_float = a.astype(np.float64, copy=False)\n        a_padded = np.pad(a_float, pad_width, mode='constant',\n                          constant_values=np.nan)\n    else:\n        a_padded = a.astype(np.float64, copy=False)\n\n    padded_len = a_padded.shape[axis]\n\n    # Build the output by iterating over windows\n    out_shape = list(a_padded.shape)\n    out_shape[axis] = out_len\n    out = np.empty(out_shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    # Use np.median (which handles NaN via ignoring if using nanmedian) for\n    # each window slice along the axis.\n    # For modes with NaN padding we use np.nanmedian.\n    _median_func = np.nanmedian if (pad_before > 0 or pad_after > 0) else np.median\n\n    for i in range(out_len):\n        sl = [slice(None)] * nd\n        sl[axis] = slice(i, i + window_size)\n        window_data = a_padded[tuple(sl)]\n        out_sl = [slice(None)] * nd\n        out_sl[axis] = i\n        out[tuple(out_sl)] = _median_func(window_data, axis=axis)\n\n    return out\n","numLines":160,"startLine":1,"totalLines":160}}}
